    Some people are saying that the "cafe mode" feature is pointless because lo-fi tracks exist, but let me make a good point that turns the tables, it's a very obvious point to make and highlights why that idea is more less wrong, and kinda stupid.

First off, I've listened to Lo-fi music before on my Sony XM5's, and straight up, it does not sound like I am in a cafe, so you either have questionable hearing, or poor awareness, I dunno, your pick. Second, you do know that speakers and headsets can fire sound in slightly different directions if support for such a feature is coded into the software, right? 

Lastly, this is not the reason someone is buying theseğŸ˜‚ But who know's? For instance, I'm going to try this feature, but I am more excited by the fact that they actually brought back the OG collapsable design, managed to make ANC better, and the sound is better too, which brings me to another point.

NO, EQ can NOT make your headset sound the same, why? Because it's not the EQ that is the main character here, it is, once again, the drivers in the headset. Depending on your drivers, certain EQ settings can actually make it sound worse because your drivers cannot accurately recreate the frequencies you are hoping for, and sometimes it works, but it can sound muddy. So the fact they were able to improve the drivers makes a big difference from the already amazing XM5's, Is a surprise because corporations like Sony usually barely change anything in their products. I Remember watching reviews on the XM5's, and tech channels were using the flat, base EQ. This means they listened to them the way they sound out of the box, so there is no bias, and they were right because my experience matched what they were talking about.

So anyway, I will hopefully be getting mine, and I hope I am not wrong here. Good thing I can always hit that return button and explain things that might make Sony try harder next time. Thank God sound is one of the harder things to fake, because of how "fragile" sound waves can be, especially when it's coming from a very small space.

    Watching this in late 2025 and the XM4 is still the GOAT.. at least for me. 

The fact that Sony brought the folding hinge back for the XM6 just proves the XM4 design was right all along. 
You get 90% of the performance for half the price. (Putting fresh earpads helps)."

State of Sony headphones in 2025:
XM6 ($450): Great, but expensive. Proof that folding headphones are superior. 
XM5 ($350): The awkward middle child. Doesn't fold, huge case.
XM4 ($200): The Value King. Still top-tier ANC and sound for nearly half the price. Great value, classic foldable design, and punchy bass.

If you own XM4s, you're not missing out. You're just saving money.

XM4 already supports LDAC (Sony's high-quality audio codec). 
You aren't missing out on major sound quality features by sticking with the older model.

Even in 2025, XM4 beat the XM5 on design (folding) and beat the XM6 on price. 
The XM4s are the Windows 7 of headphones.

One of the best tech investment I've made.

    â†³ @MikkoRantalainen  ğŸ‘0  2025-05-16
    The problem with Bluetooth is that we still do not have any better headset protocol in the Bluetooth baseline spec than we had a couple of decades ago.

Modern Bluetooth would have enough bandwidth to *always* support 48 kHz PCM audio to the headset and mono 48 kHz PCM audio from mic to the host device. However, the protocol doesn't guarantee such protocol so device manufacturers do not create support for it.

The only thing you can trust to always work is year 1998 SBC audio which is roughly GSM phone quality.

    â†³ @Paroque28  ğŸ‘0  2025-05-16
    This should not be a problem after Bluetooth 5.2

    â†³ @Jman008ful  ğŸ‘0  2025-05-16
    From Vietnamese perspective this sounds like an insult

    â†³ @MikkoRantalainen  ğŸ‘0  2025-05-16
    @Paroque28 Unfortunately, all the improved audio features are still *optional* even with Bluetooth 5.2. LC3 may or may not be supported and SBC is still the "best" you may end up with if you only look for "Bluetooth 5.2" without reading actual reviews about the real world hardware compatibility between devices.

    â†³ @evildude109  ğŸ‘0  2025-05-30
    This isn't the fault of the device, it's a fault of the bluetooth standard.  It has enough bandwidth to do pretty darn good audio one way, but really bad audio two way.  This is why some headphones actually have two different modes when you look at them in your computer's sound mixer, one "headphone" and one "headset", where the headset is garbage audio quality because it's half width.  The only thing that will fix this is for a bluetooth revision with more bandwidth to become the industry standard.
